  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ce7d2024-acf3-4793-8d41-1d6848f9aba9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer5230596394395367877">After the tumultuous events of last winter, Kate, Michael, and Emma long to continue the hunt for their missing parents. But they themselves are now in great danger, and so the wizard Stanislaus Pym hides the children at the Edgar Allan Poe Home for Hopeless and Incorrigible Orphans. There, he says, they will be safe. How wrong he is. <br/><br/> The children are soon discovered by t</span>
  <span id="freeText5230596394395367877" style="display:none">After the tumultuous events of last winter, Kate, Michael, and Emma long to continue the hunt for their missing parents. But they themselves are now in great danger, and so the wizard Stanislaus Pym hides the children at the Edgar Allan Poe Home for Hopeless and Incorrigible Orphans. There, he says, they will be safe. How wrong he is. <br /><br /> The children are soon discovered by their enemies, and a frantic chase sends Kate a hundred years into the past, to a perilous, enchanted New York City. Searching for a way back to her brother and sister, she meets a mysterious boy whose fate is intricately—and dangerously—tied to her own.<br /><br /> Meanwhile, Michael and Emma have set off to find the second of the Books of Beginning. A series of clues leads them into a hidden world where they must brave harsh polar storms, track down an ancient order of warriors, and confront terrible monsters. Will Michael and Emma find the legendary book of fire—and master its powers—before Kate is lost to them forever? <br /><br /> Exciting, suspenseful, and brimming with humor and heart, the next installment of the bestselling Books of Beginning trilogy will lead Kate, Michael, and Emma closer to their family—and to the magic that could save, or destroy, them all.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_423653549" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423653549" />
    <a title="Jeff Raymond" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32271-jeff-raymond"><img alt="Jeff Raymond" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283653266p2/32271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423653549?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff Raymond" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff Raymond" href="/user/show/32271-jeff-raymond">Jeff Raymond</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32271-jeff-raymond?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32271-jeff-raymond?shelf=read-middle-grade">read-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32271-jeff-raymond?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423653549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3321856259460979425">Putting aside <i>Harry Potter</i>, the landscape of children's fantasy is...strange. You have your classics (<i>Redwall</i>, various magical series from Lloyd Alexander, <i>Fablehaven</i>, etc), plenty of modern attempts to replicate <i>Harry Potter</i> or Tolkien (<i>Eragon</i>, anyone?). The modern stuff in particular repeatedly leaves me cold, though. Especially when you're looking for fantasy books with appeal to all genders, since most of the middle grade fiction that's not about sports or various wimpy/nerdy children is gea</span>
  <span id="freeText3321856259460979425" style="display:none">Putting aside <i>Harry Potter</i>, the landscape of children's fantasy is...strange. You have your classics (<i>Redwall</i>, various magical series from Lloyd Alexander, <i>Fablehaven</i>, etc), plenty of modern attempts to replicate <i>Harry Potter</i> or Tolkien (<i>Eragon</i>, anyone?). The modern stuff in particular repeatedly leaves me cold, though. Especially when you're looking for fantasy books with appeal to all genders, since most of the middle grade fiction that's not about sports or various wimpy/nerdy children is geared, intentionally or otherwise, toward girls, you really end up wanting something to fill that gap.<br /><br /><i>The Books of Beginning</i> are absolutely some of the best middle grade fantasy written in the last decade, and not nearly enough people know it.<br /><br /><i>The Emerald Atlas</i> is a book I got to read an advance of a few years ago, and it blew my mind. A fully-formed setting, a book that didn't mind borrowing from existing tropes while finding its own voice, kids who a) acted like kids and b) were allowed to grow into their own during the course of the book. Actions had consequences for everyone involved, and it wasn't a standard heroic journey arc for me. It felt epic for an adult, and I can only imagine what it was like for a kid looking for that same epic quality.<br /><br /><i>The Fire Chronicle</i> is the long-overdue sequel. It takes place a little while after <i>Atlas</i>, but ultimately wastes no time. The <i>Atlas</i> itself is used and misused to expected <i>and</i> unexpected consequences, we see the story progress to the next viable part, and we <i>again</i> see the kids act and grow as one would expect. The voices are genuine, the story unique while being respectfully derivative, and the plot again takes chances you don't normally see in children's literature. A <i>massive</i> breath of fresh air.<br /><br />I have no idea how <i>The Emerald Atlas</i> did, but I know it was buzzed about constantly prior to publication and then I basically never heard about it again. I'm really hoping <i>The Fire Chronicle</i> renews interest in the series, because this is one I'm looking forward to sharing with my future spawn and with people who love fantasy, because it's really a hidden gem across the board.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3321856259460979425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_556040536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556040536" />
    <a title="Jeffrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/747648-jeffrey"><img alt="Jeffrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1270218742p2/747648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/556040536?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey" href="/user/show/747648-jeffrey">Jeffrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/747648-jeffrey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/747648-jeffrey?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/747648-jeffrey?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556040536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1245000537198421906">After the huge success of Harry Potter, there has been a veritable explosion of fantasy novels aimed at the youth market. But like Harry Potter, some of these books have crossover appeal to teens and even adults.<br/><br/>A case in point is John Stephens enjoyable series "The Books of Beginning", which had its start in April 2011 with the publication of the first book in the series "The Emerald Atlas". In Stephens capable hands, this fantasy comes alive and shines. If you have not had a chance to read it,</span>
  <span id="freeText1245000537198421906" style="display:none">After the huge success of Harry Potter, there has been a veritable explosion of fantasy novels aimed at the youth market. But like Harry Potter, some of these books have crossover appeal to teens and even adults.<br /><br />A case in point is John Stephens enjoyable series "The Books of Beginning", which had its start in April 2011 with the publication of the first book in the series "The Emerald Atlas". In Stephens capable hands, this fantasy comes alive and shines. If you have not had a chance to read it, or your kids are looking for something different than the upteen sequel in the Rick Riordan's series, then you should definitely try these books. <br /><br />The Emerald Atlas, in which we are introduced to Kate, Michael and Emma, three orphan children, who had been shifted time and time again to worst and worst orphanages, were children of destiny, who were bound to find the Books of Beginning. In that first book, ably summarized by the author herein, the three children met Stanislau Pym, a wizard, discovered the first of the books of beginning --an old green book that had the power to move people back in time or stop it on a dime, and Kate learned how to use it. The children fought evil monsters and a witch, met dwarves and were all heroes. <br /><br />As we start The Fire Chronicle, the children are once again hiding out at another terrible orphanage in Maryland, when they come under attack from some monsters. Kate uses the Atlas and is transported back in time, while Michael and Emma meet Pym again and try to follow the clues to find the second Book of Beginning.<br /><br />Stephens moves back and forth between Kate's story in the past (around the time of Separation when the magical creatures and magical humans of the world wove a great spell so that non magical mundanes of the world could not see them anymore) and Michael and Emma's search for the Fire Chronicle.<br /><br />Michael, who is plagued by doubts about his worthiness must somehow overcome his fears and become the Keeper of the Book, but even before that, he, Emma, Pym and Gabriel, are attacked and have close calls aplenty while searching for the Book, must fight off Rourke, the evil henchman of the main villian in the books, the Dire Magnus, meet some elves, find a dragon guarding a treasure, and an elven princess.<br /><br />Meanwhile in the past, Kate is thrown in with some magical orphan thieves and meets Rafe, a boy of destiny. <br /><br />Stephens reveals more about the history of the world, the Dire Magnus's origins and just when you think the story is going to have a happy sort of ending, leaves you with a nice little cliffhanger.<br /><br />Its all great fantasy for youths, and this adult as well.<br /><br />The characters are deeper than you expect, with real fears and emotions. The plot is twisty, and even for a quest novel, there are plenty of surprises and action.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1245000537198421906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13301560110605479253">I actually enjoyed this book more than the first one. Probably because, of the siblings, my favorite is Michael and this is his story. I was about to give this 5 stars ... until I read the ending. Yes, I know it's not a bad ending but knowing the third book won't come out until next year (please let it be next year!) was kind of a downer. I WANT TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS NEXT!!! lol. <br/><br/>When I said on my Emerald Atlas review that Emma was the least I liked ... I take it back lol. She really grew on me a</span>
  <span id="freeText13301560110605479253" style="display:none">I actually enjoyed this book more than the first one. Probably because, of the siblings, my favorite is Michael and this is his story. I was about to give this 5 stars ... until I read the ending. Yes, I know it's not a bad ending but knowing the third book won't come out until next year (please let it be next year!) was kind of a downer. I WANT TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS NEXT!!! lol. <br /><br />When I said on my Emerald Atlas review that Emma was the least I liked ... I take it back lol. She really grew on me and I thought she was cute. I also liked that there is more to the story now than just finding the three books.<br /><br />Anyhoo, the book is a bit predictable in some areas (like Rafe's destiny) but that wasn't so bad either because you only realize it as you read on. For die hard Harry Potter fans, yes, you will notice maybe a couple of similarities but please stop b**ching and just enjoy the story. It's not so much as the original concept but the story telling itself that I loved. I read on a novelist/screenwriter's blog that people usually come out with the same ideas but the plot develops as you write the story and I have to agree.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7641129717573789839">"The point of life is to be alive! To feel things. That means the good and the bad. There'll be pain. But also joy, and friendship and love!"<br/><br/><br/>This book. Is all that and more.<br/>Fist I wanna say that this is not the first time I read it, but the last time was 2 years ago, so I didn't remember a lot of stuff. And also, that I like this one much more than the The Esmerald Atlas, why?<br/>Beacuse: -I know the characters better -Michael gets the Chronicle -We know more about Dire Magnus -Dragons -Kate & Rafe </span>
  <span id="freeText7641129717573789839" style="display:none">"The point of life is to be alive! To feel things. That means the good and the bad. There'll be pain. But also joy, and friendship and love!"<br /><br /><br />This book. Is all that and more.<br />Fist I wanna say that this is not the first time I read it, but the last time was 2 years ago, so I didn't remember a lot of stuff. And also, that I like this one much more than the The Esmerald Atlas, why?<br />Beacuse: -I know the characters better -Michael gets the Chronicle -We know more about Dire Magnus -Dragons -Kate &amp; Rafe FOREVER. -And more...<br /><br />In the last book I have already talk about each character, but I will add a little more info. First Kate; I really enojy the fact that even for a moment, she was a teenager. Enojying life and speaking to Rafe there in the bar, was also kind of romantic. Michael, I LOVE YOU, well you are actually my favourite sibling at the moment, so feel grateful. And I feel like he grew up very much in this book, (perhaps because Kate was gone) he became more brave, had more empathy with Emma and the others, etc. He had a lot more of responsibilities Although all the thing with Wilamena was soooo cute and funny. <br />Hello, Rabbit.<br />And lastly Emma, and the terrible end. In this book, I found her more vulnerable, scared and more like someone of her age, depending on her brother. Constantly scared beacuse of Kate and Gabriel and Doctor Pym, etc. I love the fact that she shows her feelings and always try to fight back.<br />The whole thing of time travelling still have me completely in love; and even better if it's New York and The Separation OMG; and Rafe.<br />Rafe. That's not fair John Stephens!! Once Kate get a guy, a hot and really nice one, you turned him evil. And I was actually falling in love of her character but suddenly, BAM, he turns into Dire Magnus.<br />Another thing is, well, elves. I won't say I hate them, but I prefer dwarfs much more. Elves are real snobs, but well, brave and beautiful creatures too.<br /><br />And the end. By the Angel, it killed me. I mean I need to know what happens next. Emma and Rourke, and The Dire Magnus. And Rafe and Kate in the land of the dead. Too much for my poor head.<br />To sum up, I entirely and absolutely loved the book. It's one of my favourites from far.<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525543462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11652779760459142519">Initial thoughts:<br/><br/>1. Michael was both sweet and annoying...in that sibling/brotherly way. Lot's of great character development and introspection with his character.<br/>2. So much magic and adventure! Fun, fast-paced read. CRAZY CLIFFHANGER CHAPTERS.<br/>3. There were quite a few Dumbledore-eque moments with Dr. Pym. It was awesome. :)<br/>4. Which reminds me, there were quite a few elements that reminded me of Harry Potter and LOTR... Not too sure how I feel about that. Just something I noticed.<br/>5. Lot's of fun</span>
  <span id="freeText11652779760459142519" style="display:none">Initial thoughts:<br /><br />1. Michael was both sweet and annoying...in that sibling/brotherly way. Lot's of great character development and introspection with his character.<br />2. So much magic and adventure! Fun, fast-paced read. CRAZY CLIFFHANGER CHAPTERS.<br />3. There were quite a few Dumbledore-eque moments with Dr. Pym. It was awesome. :)<br />4. Which reminds me, there were quite a few elements that reminded me of Harry Potter and LOTR... Not too sure how I feel about that. Just something I noticed.<br />5. Lot's of fun, and interesting characters. Really added to what is already such a magical world.<br /><br /><a href="http://youtu.be/TJ6fRGMnTYo" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out my video review here!</a> </span>

I love Emma, how stubborn and brave she is, and I can't wait to see her fulfill her role in book three. I love Michael. I love how selfless he is, how determined and brave and strong. I love the bond the siblings share, and how it makes them worthy keepers of the books. I highly recommend this trilogy and cannot wait to read the conclusion!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377487583" />
    <a title="Michael Fitzgerald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/151004-michael-fitzgerald"><img alt="Michael Fitzgerald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183257343p2/151004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377487583?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Fitzgerald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Fitzgerald" href="/user/show/151004-michael-fitzgerald">Michael Fitzgerald</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9780307879813" href="/book/show/13531478-the-fire-chronicle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377487583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8948611393938483441">The potentially powerful aspects of this story - taking on the sins of another - are squandered by the juvenile crap and dreadful touchy-feely presentation. "Choose life!" What is this, the gospel according to George Michael? <br/><br/>The star of this book is Michael, but he is a very unappealing character and (partly through Jim Dale's narration) the elf princess is awful in her syrupy sappiness. The elf vs. dwarf dichotomy is very poorly translated from Tolkien via the LOTR movies and reaches a new low</span>
  <span id="freeText8948611393938483441" style="display:none">The potentially powerful aspects of this story - taking on the sins of another - are squandered by the juvenile crap and dreadful touchy-feely presentation. "Choose life!" What is this, the gospel according to George Michael? <br /><br />The star of this book is Michael, but he is a very unappealing character and (partly through Jim Dale's narration) the elf princess is awful in her syrupy sappiness. The elf vs. dwarf dichotomy is very poorly translated from Tolkien via the LOTR movies and reaches a new low here. <br /><br />Dale also gives us Jimmy Durante impressions that do not serve the presentation well. I am still puzzled by the contradiction of the Englishness of the narration and the American setting (Baltimore, New York City). <br /><br />The NYC Chinatown sounds a bit too much like the present day. I'm skeptical that in 1899 (if it existed in the form described) it would be welcoming to soup-slurping outsiders.<br /><br />The Kate storyline is the best, but things go downhill too quickly. I wish this trilogy focused only on her. We get hammered over the head with the extolling of sibling love - it's just too much. Other points of climax are very predictable. And yes, the Potter is strong in this one. So much Voldemort - or is it Darth Vader? And then it seems that every big fight has its "Fly, you fools!" moment. So much Gandalf. Not a whole lot of originality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8948611393938483441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1467942-miss-clark?shelf=fairytale-fantasy-sci-fi-mythology">fairytale-fantasy-sci-fi-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer419626845&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419626845" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2385056089798284528">It was over a year ago that I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8619814.The_Emerald_Atlas__The_Books_of_Beginning___1_' title='The Emerald Atlas (The Books of Beginning, #1) by John Stephens' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emerald Atlas</a> and the length of time separating these two books could not have helped how I viewed this one. Still, even without coming to this volume fresh from the first, I found this one less enjoyable for three core reasons.<br/><br/>1. I did not understand (and still am failing to grasp) the manner in which the Dire Magnus is perpetuating his life.<br/><br/><blockquote>The life of the universe is not a straight line. Rather, imagine a circle. And along the circle, the universe is bor</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2385056089798284528" style="display:none">It was over a year ago that I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8619814.The_Emerald_Atlas__The_Books_of_Beginning___1_" title="The Emerald Atlas (The Books of Beginning, #1) by John Stephens" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emerald Atlas</a> and the length of time separating these two books could not have helped how I viewed this one. Still, even without coming to this volume fresh from the first, I found this one less enjoyable for three core reasons.<br /><br />1. I did not understand (and still am failing to grasp) the manner in which the Dire Magnus is perpetuating his life.<br /><br /><blockquote>The life of the universe is not a straight line. Rather, imagine a circle. And along the circle, the universe is born, destroys itself, and is born again, over and over, endlessly. Just as the universe is reborn over and over, so is everything in it. And what the Dire Magnus did was to make contact with those earlier versions of the universe, to reach into them and pluck out his other selves and bring them here. But then he threw these other selves out across time, each further than the last, like stones tossed into the ocean, so that every few hundred years, another would be born into this world.</blockquote><br /><br />So, the Dire Magnus creates this so-called "living bridge" and as each Magnus grows old, he has to go find his younger self and transfer his memories and power to that one. I am sorry, but I just don't understand it and thus I am severely frustrated.<br /><br />2. Love interest and future Dire Magnus Rafe. I did not find myself emotionally connected to Rafe at all. Jake and Beetles were more endearing. His instant attraction for Katherine to the point of giving himself up to become the person who will kill hundreds all in pursuit of power is just sad. *frustration level increases*<br /><br />3. For no particular reason, I was simply not as engaged with Katherine, Emma and Michael in this one. The story did not go in the direction that I thought it would.<br /><br /><br />I <b>did</b> really like Michael's character development and Princess Wilamina and her elves. That was about it. It was another middle book that felt like if it was more tightly plotted could have been just two books. I will <i>probably</i> read the final book...</span>
  <a data-text-id="2385056089798284528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8772687658473641325">Since I gave <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247497000' rel='nofollow noopener'>the first book</a> in this series four stars, I feel I simply must give this one five, as the series merits at least four and this second book in the trilogy may, in fact, and most unusually, be even better than the first. It really deserves much more buzz than has come my way, and many more readers. I'm going to have to find more ways to highlight and recommend the series while we wait for the final installment.<br/><br/>Early on, this book gives a nice little summary of the first one (though th</span>
  <span id="freeText8772687658473641325" style="display:none">Since I gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247497000" rel="nofollow noopener">the first book</a> in this series four stars, I feel I simply must give this one five, as the series merits at least four and this second book in the trilogy may, in fact, and most unusually, be even better than the first. It really deserves much more buzz than has come my way, and many more readers. I'm going to have to find more ways to highlight and recommend the series while we wait for the final installment.<br /><br />Early on, this book gives a nice little summary of the first one (though these bare bones hardly capture how nicely the story fleshes out):<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Frustrated at having had her hair pulled for the third time in one week, Emma had suggested that they tell Miss Crumley the truth: that Dr. Stanislaus Pym was a wizard, that the reason Miss Crumley couldn't find Cambridge Falls on a map was that it was part of the magical world and therefore hidden from normal (or in her case, subnormal) humans, that as far as what had happened there, the three of them had discovered an old book bound in green leather that had carried them back through time, that they'd met dwarves and monsters, fought an evil witch, saved an entire town, and that pretty much any way you looked at it, they were heroes. Even Michael.</i>
</blockquote>The three siblings are back in an orphanage at the start of this book while Dr. Pym is unexpectedly away on business, but they know that the Dire Magnus is still looking for them and that their quest for the Books of Beginning must continue. Oldest sister Kate has bonded with the time-traveling Emerald Atlas, so now they must find the books for Michael and Emma before the Dire Magnus's minions to fulfill their destiny and save the world. The adventure just gets bigger and the stakes get larger as they go.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9278921701667589634">I wasn't overly thrilled with <i>The Emerald Atlas</i> and even less so with this middle-of-the-trilogy book; the influences of Rowling, Tolkein, Lewis and others was just so overt and the new blend didn't work for me.<br/><br/>Example? A Big Bad who is supposed to be dead, but somehow still lives in an incorporeal form (and is looking to find a "new" body). Example? A world of magic and a world of 'normal' that exist side-by-side but with the normals not realizing (at least, they don't after the Great Separatio</span>
  <span id="freeText9278921701667589634" style="display:none">I wasn't overly thrilled with <i>The Emerald Atlas</i> and even less so with this middle-of-the-trilogy book; the influences of Rowling, Tolkein, Lewis and others was just so overt and the new blend didn't work for me.<br /><br />Example? A Big Bad who is supposed to be dead, but somehow still lives in an incorporeal form (and is looking to find a "new" body). Example? A world of magic and a world of 'normal' that exist side-by-side but with the normals not realizing (at least, they don't after the Great Separation). <br /><br />Now that they have the Atlas, the Wibberly's are back at the Baltimore orphanage they hate; events conspire to separate them, sending Kate to turn-of-the-century New York and Michael and Emma first to Italy, then to Tierra del Fuego and on to Antarctica and a hidden valley. The Fire Chronicle is the second of the Books they're looking for, more properly known as the Book of Life - and they're looking for the final book, the Book of Death. <br /><br />I won't be on the quest with them.<br /><br />ARC provided by publisher. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jiZYpNgtKaxogemaNCtvDWIkkYlsn+ys6vZw7mdffQSaOIYRS+lNfp/FlJ97Y50tY4jStphCSI+0aX1NqOggJA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/3/CdGuwmLfwo9JwpHFXtQpdaVheVwlDUJVpcI0bofXrYRzB+HT8ZQfnr3XrOaWVC/EqZ6qKrWAOCmTTQqz81Q==')})
  }
